<span id="freeTextContainer9619511185975723454">This review has also been cross-posted on my <a href='http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2013/01/31/the-serpents-shadow-by-rick-riordan/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Happy Indulgence Blog</a>, check it out for more reviews! <br/><br/>Carter and Sadie Kane are descendents of the House of Life, an Egyptian temple of magic. In The Red Pyramid and The Throne of Fire, the Kanes learnt to command their unique abilities and revived the sun god Ra, a worthy opponent to the god of chaos, Apophis. In the third and final installment of this electrifying trilogy, Apophis is hell bent on bringing forth the end of days, and the Kanes have a </span>
  <span id="freeText9619511185975723454" style="display:none">This review has also been cross-posted on my <a href="http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2013/01/31/the-serpents-shadow-by-rick-riordan/" rel="nofollow noopener">Happy Indulgence Blog</a>, check it out for more reviews! <br /><br />Carter and Sadie Kane are descendents of the House of Life, an Egyptian temple of magic. In The Red Pyramid and The Throne of Fire, the Kanes learnt to command their unique abilities and revived the sun god Ra, a worthy opponent to the god of chaos, Apophis. In the third and final installment of this electrifying trilogy, Apophis is hell bent on bringing forth the end of days, and the Kanes have a limited amount of time to defeat the god of Chaos himself and save mankind.<br /><br />Following on from the Percy Jackson phenomenon about Greek gods and their offspring, the Kane Chronicles breathes life into the Egyptian gods and goddesses. From an off-kilter exuberant hippopotamus epitomising Hapi, the god of the Nile and an incredibly feline and agile female depicting Bast, the cat goddess, Riordan’s creativity shines as he interprets the quirks of these ancient beings.<br /><br />The Serpent’s Shadow picks up where The Throne of Fire left off, as Carter and Sadie discover an ancient spell that may defeat Apophis. With magical abilities and an academy of magical students, these siblings have the weight of the world on their shoulders. Told through interchanging perspectives, we learn about Sadie’s inner turmoil between two boys, and Carter’s insecurities about his role as a leader.<br /><br />It’s the creativity and immensely imaginative world that Riordan has created that’s the focus here, and you’ll be constantly entertained with The Serpent’s Shadow. Whether we’re stumbling upon the next Egyptian god, hearing from Sadie’s ghostly mother, visiting the underworld or seeing Carter turning into a falcon, The Serpent’s Shadow is full of surprises.<br /><br />You’d definitely need to read the first two books of the Kane Chronicles before delving into this one, as it’s full steam ahead from the first chapter. If you’ve read the Percy Jackson series and you’re hankering for more, or you simply love Egypt, this series will not disappoint and you’ll be wondering why it’s just a trilogy.<br /><br />I received a review copy of the book from the publisher in exchange for an honest review.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8851395241587394546">1- This five star rating I gave this book, is not the same 5-star that I gave The Lord of Rings or Blindness or many other books. So this doesn't necessarily mean that this book can be compared to them. It's just means that the book was as good as I expected it to be. <br/><br/>2- I - MOSTLY - like the romances and the relationships in Riordan's books. They're cute and not much unbearable. Stories of Sadie with Anubis/Walt and Carter with Zia was good and understandable, even when <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ they tur</span></span>
  <span id="freeText8851395241587394546" style="display:none">1- This five star rating I gave this book, is not the same 5-star that I gave The Lord of Rings or Blindness or many other books. So this doesn't necessarily mean that this book can be compared to them. It's just means that the book was as good as I expected it to be. <br /><br />2- I - MOSTLY - like the romances and the relationships in Riordan's books. They're cute and not much unbearable. Stories of Sadie with Anubis/Walt and Carter with Zia was good and understandable, even when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ they turn out to be gods, or at least become gods.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But still, the best relationship in the whole book was between Carter and Sadie. I like the bonds that shapes between brothers and sisters in tough times. When, for example, in the last book Sadie confronted that she will die for her brother's sake, if necessary. That bond developed in this book in a very beautiful way. I loved their feelings... <br /><br />+ Alright, I have to say this, I understand Sadie. Walt WAS cute. So was Anubis, by the way. :D<br /><br />3- I have no idea why, but Riordan seems to have an unconditional love for deadlines. " The world shall end in two days if you don't do something. ". It's horrible. It repeats and repeats in every book. Seriously, WHY?<br /><br />4- One of the most important reasons why I keep reading his books, is that the modern teenagers are modern teenagers. They talk about Hunger Games and behave like they are people in the 21st century. <br /><br />5- Most important point is that Rick Riordan knows how to make a joke. He IS funny. I could give all the five stars to all the amazing jokes. <br /><br /><i>There’s my baby!” I cried, quite carried away. “There’s my Poochiekins!”<br />Ammit ran at me and leaped into my arms, nuzzling me with his rough snout.<br />“My lord Osiris!” Disturber lost the bottom of his scroll again, which unraveled around his legs. “This is an outrage!”<br />“Sadie,” Dad said firmly, “please do not refer to the Devourer of Souls as Poochiekins.</i> <br /><br />+ I just put the laptop down and laughed at this. I couldn't afford it breaking :))))</span>

<div id="review_1578630481" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1578630481" />
    <a title="Jules ♈  (witchyrover)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44480390-jules-witchyrover"><img alt="Jules ♈  (witchyrover)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578182465p2/44480390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1578630481?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jules ♈  (witchyrover)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jules ♈  (witchyrover)" href="/user/show/44480390-jules-witchyrover">Jules ♈  (witchyrover)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781423142027" href="/book/show/17193778-the-serpent-s-shadow">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">egyptian-gods and rick lovers</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1578630481" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17397335538264168956">The Serpent's Shadow is the third and last installment of the Kane Chronicles Series. An end-of-the-world scenario that must be fixed by the Kane teens before the bad guy, Apophis, deals up a huge blow to life as we know it. It’s a recipe for high adventure and self-discovery for Carter and Sadie, who have been thrust into roles well beyond their wildest imagination in the first two books. Now it’s time to lay everything on the line and seal the deal.<br/><br/>To be honest, it took me a while to get my ha</span>
  <span id="freeText17397335538264168956" style="display:none">The Serpent's Shadow is the third and last installment of the Kane Chronicles Series. An end-of-the-world scenario that must be fixed by the Kane teens before the bad guy, Apophis, deals up a huge blow to life as we know it. It’s a recipe for high adventure and self-discovery for Carter and Sadie, who have been thrust into roles well beyond their wildest imagination in the first two books. Now it’s time to lay everything on the line and seal the deal.<br /><br />To be honest, it took me a while to get my hands on this book as I did not enjoy the second as much as I enjoyed the first. However, I am glad I did as it did not disappoint. Exciting, fast-paced, and brilliantly executed, the newest, and last, book in the trilogy wraps up the story of Sadie and Carter Kane, squabbling siblings who have each other's back, no matter what. <br /><br /><i> “It takes strength and courage to admit the truth.” </i><br /><br />Riordan has a great imagination that can weave the complexities of Egyptian mythology into a story that can be understood and followed by readers. As evidenced in all of his books in this genre, he has found a way to cleverly blend the modern with the ancient, with splashes of dry wit and humorous sarcasm thrown in. Although it was definitely better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9067850.The_Throne_of_Fire__The_Kane_Chronicles___2_" title="The Throne of Fire (The Kane Chronicles, #2) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Throne of Fire</a>, Sadie's boy struggle was somewhat awkward and, therefore, unnecessary in my opinion. <br /><br />This series is highly recommended to PJO and mythology fans as it is thoroughly entertaining.<br /><br />Feel free to check out my review on:<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1578630088" rel="nofollow noopener">The Red Pyramid</a> (★★★★ 1/2)<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1578630352" rel="nofollow noopener">The Throne of Fire</a> (★★★ 1/4)</span>
  <a data-text-id="17397335538264168956" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_214253563" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/214253563" />
    <a title="Mith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3620424-mith"><img alt="Mith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389091865p2/3620424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/214253563?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mith" href="/user/show/3620424-mith">Mith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3620424-mith?shelf=absolutely-spiffing">absolutely-spiffing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3620424-mith?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3620424-mith?shelf=wizards-n-dragons">wizards-n-dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3620424-mith?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer214253563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9085434161017251286"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Well that was a fun ride! Having started off sluggishly, the (supposed) trilogy didn't exactly end with a bang, but there were quite some fireworks in there nonetheless.<br/><br/>I say "supposed" because the very last paragraph in the book hints at a Heroes Of Olympus/Kane Chronicles crossover (I have a feeling we're going to run into Setne and the Book of Thoth pretty soon - say, September 2012?)! That should be interesting :)</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_331083111" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/331083111" />
    <a title="K." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/861629-k"><img alt="K." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1342794238p2/861629.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/331083111?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K." class="user" itemprop="url" name="K." href="/user/show/861629-k">K.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer331083111" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4007082398922160792">Just read this with the kids. I still love Carter & Sadie, the plot was well done, interesting and fun, writing funny, etc. Sometimes it had me in stitches (and I loved hearing my 10yo giggle her head off reading it). Riordan creates the funniest chapter headings since I don't know who. <br/><br/>However, I still DON'T love the very early teen romance. Riordan seemed to do better with Carter & Zia in this one, it was light and puppy-ish and more about friendship. Sadie and her two lovers were a different </span>
  <span id="freeText4007082398922160792" style="display:none">Just read this with the kids. I still love Carter &amp; Sadie, the plot was well done, interesting and fun, writing funny, etc. Sometimes it had me in stitches (and I loved hearing my 10yo giggle her head off reading it). Riordan creates the funniest chapter headings since I don't know who. <br /><br />However, I still DON'T love the very early teen romance. Riordan seemed to do better with Carter &amp; Zia in this one, it was light and puppy-ish and more about friendship. Sadie and her two lovers were a different story. Gag. She's WAY too young, period. Not that kids don't "fall in love" but the whole dialogue was too mature and sophisticated for a barely 13 yo. It was just annoying, but I guess it'll be a good conversation with the kids. <br /><br />All in all a fun, clean, enjoyable read, which is what I'm going for right now. Riordan readers in our family can't wait to see how he ties all three of these series together. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4007082398922160792" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zFPa7qpvHjbR7LwjS9uUDhOIefymcpZdVdnCLaARoPf2dbM8ETHXXnbHCEK8Lp7RxdeeNGj/GDoOp4ScbVJSbQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Lu0ZK3xJpgxigdLj7+OCLhKLB9X3rA6aQBQXAlOR3VwUy3D5xxdvZMWqZoIYFojxxNTgHTkhgP0balGzntIvxg==')})
  }

Excerpt: The Giver is a 1993 soft science fiction novel by Lois Lowry. It is set in a future society which is at first presented as a utopian society and gradually appears more and more dystopian; therefore, it could be considered anti-utopian. The novel follows a boy named Jonas through the twelfth year of his life. The society has eliminated pain and strife by converting to &quot;Sameness,&quot; a plan which has also eradicated emotional depth from their lives. Jonas is selected to inherit the position of &quot;Receiver of Memory,&quot; the person who stores all the memories of the time before Sameness, in case they are ever needed to aid in decisions that others lack the experience to make. When Jonas meets the Giver, he is confused in many ways. The Giver is also able to break some rules, such as turning off the speaker and locking his door. As Jonas receives the memories from the previous receiverthe &quot;Giver&quot;he discovers the power of knowledge. The people in his community are happy because they don\'t know of a better life but with the knowledge of what they are missing out on it could create chaos. He faces a dilemma: Should he stay with the community, his family living a shallow life without love, color, sound and knowledge or should he run away to where he can live a full life? Despite controversy and criticism that the book\'s subject material is inappropriate for young children, The Giver won the 1994 Newbery Medal and has sold more than 5.3 million copies. In Australia, the United States and Canada, it is a part of many middle school reading lists, but it is also on many banned book lists and appeared on the American Library Association\'s list of the
